### Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 1 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A company that makes wildlife videos purchases camera equipment for $\$ 32,400$. The equipment depreciates in value at a constant rate for 12 years, after which it is considered to have no monetary value. How much is the camera equipment worth 4 years after it is purchased?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 10,800$
  B: $\$ 16,200$
  C: $\$ 21,600$
  D: $\$ 29,700$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The equipment depreciates in value at a constant rate for 12 years.
  After 12 years, the equipment is considered to have no monetary value.
  Therefore, the equipment depreciates linearly over 12 years.
  Let's use the formula for the equation of a line to find the value of the equipment after 4 years.
  We know that the initial value of the equipment is $\$ 32,400$.
  We also know that the equipment depreciates linearly over 12 years, so the rate of depreciation is $\frac{\$ 32,400 - \$ 0}{12 \text{ years}} = \$ 2,700$ per year.
  Therefore, the equation of the line that represents the value of the equipment over time is:
  $$
  V(t) = -2700t + 32400
  $$
  where $t$ is the time in years and $V(t)$ is the value of the equipment in dollars.
  To find the value of the equipment after 4 years, we can plug in $t = 4$ into the equation:
  $$
  V(4) = -2700(4) + 32400 = \$ 21,600
  $$
  Therefore, the equipment is worth $\$ 21,600$ after 4 years.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The equipment depreciates at a constant rate for 12 years.
  After 12 years, the equipment has no monetary value.
  Therefore, the equipment depreciates $\frac{\$ 32,400}{12 \text{ years}} = \$ 2,700$ per year.
  After 4 years, the equipment has depreciated $4 \times \$ 2,700 = \$ 10,800$.
  Therefore, the equipment is worth $\$ 32,400 - \$ 10,800 = \$ 21,600$ after 4 years.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Thought:
  The equipment depreciates in value at a constant rate for 12 years.
  After 12 years, the equipment is considered to have no monetary value.
  Therefore, the equipment depreciates linearly over 12 years.
  Let's find the yearly depreciation rate.
  The initial value of the equipment is $\$ 32,400$.
  After 12 years, the equipment is worth $\$ 0$.
  The yearly depreciation rate is $\frac{\$ 32,400 - \$ 0}{12 \text{ years}} = \$ 2,700$.
  After 4 years, the equipment has depreciated $\$ 2,700 \times 4 = \$ 10,800$.
  The current value of the equipment is $\$ 32,400 - \$ 10,800 = \$ 21,600$.
  Therefore, the answer is C: $\$ 21,600$.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 3:
Thought:
  The equipment depreciates at a constant rate for 12 years.
  After 12 years, the equipment is considered to have no monetary value.
  Therefore, the equipment depreciates linearly over 12 years.
  Let's use the straight-line depreciation method to calculate the depreciation per year.
  The depreciation per year is ($32,400 - 0) / 12 = $2,700.
  After 4 years, the equipment has depreciated by 4 * $2,700 = $10,800.
  The current value of the equipment is $32,400 - $10,800 = $21,600.
  Therefore, the answer is C: $\$ 21,600$.

  The current value of the equipment is the initial value minus the amount of depreciation.
  Therefore, the current value of the equipment is $\$ 32,400 - \$ 10,800 = \$ 21,600$.

Response 9:
Thought:
  The equipment depreciates in value at a constant rate for 12 years.
  After 12 years, the equipment is considered to have no monetary value.
  Therefore, the equipment depreciates linearly over 12 years.
  Let's use the straight-line depreciation method to find the annual depreciation rate.
  The initial value of the equipment is $\$ 32,400$.
  The salvage value of the equipment is $\$ 0$.
  The useful life of the equipment is 12 years.
  Annual depreciation = (Initial value - Salvage value) / Useful life
  Annual depreciation = ($\$ 32,400 - \$ 0$) / 12 = $\$ 2,700$
  After 4 years, the equipment has depreciated by 4 x $\$ 2,700$ = $\$ 10,800$
  The current value of the equipment = Initial value - Accumulated depreciation
  Current value = $\$ 32,400 - \$ 10,800$ = $\$ 21,600$
  Therefore, the answer is C: $\$ 21,600$.
Action: Answer("C")

### Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 2 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$\frac{a-b}{a}=c$$In the equation above, if $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, which of the following must be true?
Choices:
  A: $c>1$
  B: $c=1$
  C: $c=-1$
  D: $c<-1$
Response 0:
Thought:
  If $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, then $a-b$ is negative.
  Since $a$ is negative, $-a$ is positive.
  Therefore, $\frac{a-b}{a}=\frac{-1(a-b)}{-1a}=\frac{b-a}{-a}=\frac{a-b}{a}=c$.
  Since $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, $a-b$ is negative and $a+b$ is positive.
  Therefore, $a+b>a-b$.
  Dividing both sides by $a$, we get $\frac{a+b}{a}>\frac{a-b}{a}=c$.
  Simplifying, we get $1+\frac{b}{a}>c$.
  Since $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, $\frac{b}{a}$ is negative.
  Therefore, $1+\frac{b}{a}>c>-1$.
  The only choice that satisfies this inequality is A: $c>1$.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  If $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, then $a-b$ is negative.
  Since $a$ is negative, $a$ is less than 0.
  Therefore, $\frac{a-b}{a}$ is greater than 1.
  So, $c$ must be greater than 1.
  The answer is A: $c>1$.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Thought:
  If $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, then $a-b$ is negative.
  Since $a$ is negative, $-a$ is positive.
  Therefore, $\frac{a-b}{a}=\frac{-1(a-b)}{-1a}=\frac{b-a}{-a}=\frac{a-b}{a}=c$
  Since $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, $a-b$ is negative and $|a-b|=b-a$.
  If we substitute $a=-x$ and $b=y$, where $x$ and $y$ are positive numbers, we get $\frac{x+y}{-x}=c$.
  Multiplying both sides by $-x$ gives $y-xc=x+y$.
  Rearranging the terms gives $y-x=y(1-c)$.
  Since $y$ is positive, we can divide both sides by $y$ to get $1-\frac{x}{y}=1-c$.
  Therefore, $c=\frac{x}{y}$.
  Since $x$ and $y$ are positive, $c$ must be positive.
  Therefore, $c>0$.
  None of the answer choices are greater than 0.
  Therefore, the answer is "None of the Above".

  Therefore, $c$ must be negative.
  The answer is C: $c=-1$.

  Since $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, $a-b$ is negative and $|a-b|=b-a$.

  If $c=1$, then $|a-b|=a$, which is not possible since $|a-b|$ is positive and $a$ is negative.

Question: $$h(x)=2^{x}$$The function $h$ is defined above. What is $h(5)-h(3) ?$
Choices:
  A: 2
  B: 4
  C: 24
  D: 28
Response 0:
Thought:
  $h(x)=2^{x}$, so $h(5)=2^{5}=32$ and $h(3)=2^{3}=8$.
  Therefore, $h(5)-h(3)=32-8=24$.
  The answer is C: 24.
Action: Answer("C")

### Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 4 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: If $f(x)=\frac{x^{2}-6 x+3}{x-1}$, what is $f(-1)$ ?
Choices:
  A: -5
  B: -2
  C: 2
  D: 5
Response 0:
Thought:
  To find $f(-1)$, we need to substitute $-1$ for $x$ in the expression for $f(x)$.
  $f(x)=\frac{x^{2}-6 x+3}{x-1}$ can be factored as $f(x)=\frac{(x-3)(x-1)}{x-1}$.
  Since $x-1$ is a common factor in the numerator and denominator, we can simplify $f(x)$ as $f(x)=x-3$.
  Therefore, $f(-1)=-1-3=-4$.
Action: Answer("None of the Above") 

Note: None of the above is the correct answer since none of the given choices match the correct answer of -4.
Response 1:
Thought:
  To find $f(-1)$, we need to substitute $-1$ for $x$ in the function $f(x)$.
  $f(x)=\frac{x^{2}-6 x+3}{x-1}$
  $f(-1)=\frac{(-1)^{2}-6(-1)+3}{-1-1}$
  $f(-1)=\frac{1+6+3}{-2}$
  $f(-1)=\frac{10}{-2}$
  $f(-1)=-5$
  Therefore, the answer is A: -5.
Action: Answer("A")

### Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 5 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A cylindrical can containing pieces of fruit is filled to the top with syrup before being sealed. The base of the can has an area of $75 \mathrm{~cm}^{2}$, and the height of the can is $10 \mathrm{~cm}$. If $110 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$ of syrup is needed to fill the can to the top, which of the following is closest to the total volume of the pieces of fruit in the can?
Choices:
  A: $7.5 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$
  B: $185 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$
  C: $640 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$
  D: $750 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The volume of the syrup is $110 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  The height of the can is $10 \mathrm{~cm}$.
  The base of the can has an area of $75 \mathrm{~cm}^{2}$.
  Therefore, the volume of the can is $750 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  The volume of the fruit is the difference between the volume of the can and the volume of the syrup.
  Therefore, the volume of the fruit is $750 \mathrm{~cm}^{3} - 110 \mathrm{~cm}^{3} = 640 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  The answer is C: $640 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The volume of the syrup is $110 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  The height of the can is $10 \mathrm{~cm}$.
  The base of the can has an area of $75 \mathrm{~cm}^{2}$.
  The volume of the can is the product of the base area and the height.
  The volume of the fruit is the difference between the volume of the can and the volume of the syrup.
  Therefore, we can calculate the volume of the fruit by subtracting the volume of the syrup from the volume of the can.
  The volume of the can is $75 \mathrm{~cm}^{2} \times 10 \mathrm{~cm} = 750 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  The volume of the fruit is $750 \mathrm{~cm}^{3} - 110 \mathrm{~cm}^{3} = 640 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  The answer is C: $640 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.

  The volume of the fruit is the difference between the volume of the can and the volume of the syrup.
  Therefore, the volume of the fruit is $750 \mathrm{~cm}^{3} - 110 \mathrm{~cm}^{3} = 640 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  The answer is C: $640 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
Action: Answer("C")

  B: 15
  C: 20
  D: 23

  B: $(3,-8)$
  C: $(4,-6)$
  D: $(9,-6)$

### Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 10 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: If $2 w+4 t=14$ and $4 w+5 t=25$, what is the value of $2 w+3 t ?$
Choices:
  A: 6
  B: 10
  C: 13
  D: 17
Response 0:
Thought:
  We are given two equations:
  $2 w+4 t=14$  ...(1)
  $4 w+5 t=25$  ...(2)
  We need to find the value of $2 w+3 t$
  We can solve the above equations using elimination method.
  Multiplying equation (1) by 2, we get $4w + 8t = 28$.
  Multiplying equation (2) by -2, we get $-8w - 10t = -50$.
  Adding the above two equations, we get $-4t = -22$.
  Solving for $t$, we get $t = \frac{22}{4} = 5.5$.
  Substituting the value of $t$ in equation (1), we get $2w + 4(5.5) = 14$.
  Solving for $w$, we get $w = \frac{1}{2}$.
  Substituting the values of $w$ and $t$ in $2w + 3t$, we get $2(\frac{1}{2}) + 3(5.5) = 17$.
  Therefore, the value of $2w + 3t$ is 17.
  The answer is D: 17.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  We are given two equations with two variables.
  We can solve for one variable in terms of the other in both equations.
  Then we can set the two expressions equal to each other and solve for the remaining variable.
  $2 w+4 t=14$ can be simplified to $w+2t=7$ by dividing both sides by 2.
  $4 w+5 t=25$ can be simplified to $w+\frac{5}{4}t=\frac{25}{4}$ by dividing both sides by 4.
  We can then set the two expressions equal to each other and solve for $t$.
  $w+2t=7$ and $w+\frac{5}{4}t=\frac{25}{4}$
  Subtracting the first equation from the second, we get $\frac{3}{4}t=\frac{3}{4}$, so $t=1$.
  We can substitute $t=1$ into either of the original equations to solve for $w$.
  $2w+4(1)=14$ gives $w=5$.
  Finally, we can substitute $w=5$ and $t=1$ into $2w+3t$ to get the answer.
  $2(5)+3(1)=13$
  Therefore, the answer is C: 13.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Thought:
  We can solve the system of equations by elimination or substitution method.
  Let's use the elimination method.
  Multiplying the first equation by $-2$ and adding it to the second equation eliminates $w$.
  We get $-7t = -3$, which gives $t = \frac{3}{7}$.
  Substituting $t$ in the first equation gives $w = 2$.
  Therefore, $2w+3t = 2(2) + 3\left(\frac{3}{7}\right) = \frac{25}{7}$.
  The answer is not one of the available choices, so the closest answer is C: 13.

Choices:
  A: 18
  B: 20
  C: 24
  D: 40

  $$5a x^3 + (20a - ab + 15) x^2 + (-4ab - 3b + 12a) x + 12 = 20 x^{3}-9 x^{2}-2 x+12$$
  We can equate the coefficients of each term on both sides of the equation.
  For the coefficient of $x^3$, we have $5a = 20$, which gives us $a = 4$.
  For the constant term, we have $12 = 12$, which is true for any value of $a$ and $b$.
  For the coefficient of $x^2$, we have $20a - ab + 15 = -9$, which gives us $ab = -11$.
  For the coefficient of $x$, we have $-4ab - 3b + 12a = -2$, which gives us $b = \frac{2}{11}$.
  Therefore, $ab = 4 \times \frac{2}{11} = \frac{8}{11}$.

Question: If $a^{2}+b^{2}=z$ and $a b=y$, which of the following is equivalent to $4 z+8 y$ ?
Choices:
  A: $(a+2 b)^{2}$
  B: $(2 a+2 b)^{2}$
  C: $(4 a+4 b)^{2}$
  D: $(4 a+8 b)^{2}$
Response 0:
Thought:
We are given that $a^2+b^2=z$ and $ab=y$.
We need to find an expression equivalent to $4z+8y$.
We can factor out 4 from $4z$ and 8 from $8y$ to get $4(z+2y)$.
We can substitute $z=a^2+b^2$ and $y=ab$ to get $4(a^2+b^2+2ab)$.
We can simplify the expression inside the parentheses to get $4(a+b)^2$.
Therefore, the expression equivalent to $4z+8y$ is $(2a+2b)^2$.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
We are given $a^{2}+b^{2}=z$ and $a b=y$.
We need to find an expression equivalent to $4 z+8 y$.
We can rewrite $4 z+8 y$ as $4(a^{2}+b^{2})+8(a b)$.
We can factor out 4 from the expression to get $4(a^{2}+2ab+b^{2})$.
We can then use the identity $a^{2}+2 a b+b^{2}=(a+b)^{2}$.
Therefore, $4(a^{2}+2ab+b^{2})=4(a+b)^{2}$.
Option A is not equivalent to $4 z+8 y$.
Option B is not equivalent to $4 z+8 y$.
Option C is not equivalent to $4 z+8 y$.
Option D can be simplified as $(4a+8b)^2 = 16(a+2b)^2$.
Therefore, the answer is D: $(4 a+8 b)^{2}$.

Question: Shipping Charges\begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|c|c|}\hline$\begin{array}{c}\text { Merchandise weight } \\ \text { (pounds) }\end{array}$ & $\begin{array}{c}\text { Shipping } \\ \text { charge }\end{array}$ \\\hline5 & $\$ 16.94$ \\\hline10 & $\$ 21.89$ \\\hline20 & $\$ 31.79$ \\\hline40 & $\$ 51.59$ \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}The table above shows shipping charges for an online retailer that sells sporting goods. There is a linear relationship between the shipping charge and the weight of the merchandise. Which function can be used to determine the total shipping charge $f(x)$, in dollars, for an order with a merchandise weight of $x$ pounds?
Choices:
  A: $f(x)=0.99 x$
  B: $f(x)=0.99 x+11.99$
  C: $f(x)=3.39 x$
  D: $f(x)=3.39 x+16.94$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The function is linear, so it can be written in the form of $f(x)=mx+b$, where $m$ is the slope and $b$ is the y-intercept.
  The slope of the function is equal to the rate of change of the shipping charge per pound of merchandise weight.
  The y-intercept of the function is the shipping charge when the merchandise weight is zero.
  Using the given table, we can calculate the slope and y-intercept of the function.
  The slope is equal to the change in shipping charge divided by the change in merchandise weight.
  The y-intercept is the shipping charge when the merchandise weight is zero, which is $\$16.94$.
  Therefore, the function is $f(x)=3.39x+16.94$.
  The answer is D: $f(x)=3.39 x+16.94$.
Action: Answer("D")

### Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 18 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: \begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|c|c|c|c|}\hline$x$ & $a$ & $3 a$ & $5 a$ \\\hline$y$ & 0 & $-a$ & $-2 a$ \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}Some values of $x$ and their corresponding values of $y$ are shown in the table above, where $a$ is a constant. If there is a linear relationship between $x$ and $y$, which of the following equations represents the relationship?
Choices:
  A: $x+2 y=a$
  B: $x+2 y=5 a$
  C: $2 x-y=-5 a$
  D: $2 x-y=7 a$
Response 0:
Thought:
  To determine the linear relationship between $x$ and $y$, we can use the formula for the equation of a line, $y=mx+b$, where $m$ is the slope and $b$ is the y-intercept.
  We can find the slope by calculating the change in $y$ over the change in $x$ between two points on the line.
  Let's choose the points $(a,0)$ and $(3a,-a)$ from the table.
  The change in $y$ is $-a-0=-a$, and the change in $x$ is $3a-a=2a$.
  Therefore, the slope is $m=\frac{-a}{2a}=-\frac{1}{2}$.
  We can find the y-intercept by plugging in one of the points and the slope into the formula and solving for $b$.
  Let's use the point $(a,0)$.
  We have $0=-\frac{1}{2}(a)+b$, so $b=\frac{1}{2}a$.
  Therefore, the equation of the line is $y=-\frac{1}{2}x+\frac{1}{2}a$.
  We can simplify this equation by multiplying both sides by $-2$ to get $-2y=x-a$.
  This equation matches choice A, so the answer is A: $x+2y=a$. 
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  We can find the slope of the line using two points from the table.
  Let's use the first and second rows of the table.
  The slope of the line is $\frac{-a-0}{3a-a}=-1$.
  The equation of the line in slope-intercept form is $y=-x+b$.
  We can find the y-intercept by plugging in the coordinates of one of the points.
  Let's use the first row of the table.
  $0=-1(0)+b$.
  $b=0$.
  Therefore, the equation of the line is $y=-x$.
  We can rewrite this equation as $x+y=0$.
  We can multiply both sides by $-1$ to get $x+(-y)=0$.
  Therefore, the equation of the line is $2x-y=0$.
  We can multiply both sides by $-5$ to get $2x-y=-5a$.
  Therefore, the answer is C: $2x-y=-5a$.

  Since there is a linear relationship between $x$ and $y$, we can use the slope-intercept form of a linear equation, $y=mx+b$, where $m$ is the slope and $b$ is the y-intercept.
  The slope of the line passing through $(a,0)$ and $(3a,-a)$ is $\frac{-a-0}{3a-a}=-\frac{a}{2a}=-\frac{1}{2}$.
  The equation of the line passing through $(a,0)$ and $(3a,-a)$ is $y=-\frac{1}{2}x+\frac{3}{2}a$.
  The slope of the line passing through $(3a,-a)$ and $(5a,-2a)$ is $\frac{-2a+a}{5a-3a}=-\frac{a}{2a}=-\frac{1}{2}$.
  The equation of the line passing through $(3a,-a)$ and $(5a,-2a)$ is $y=-\frac{1}{2}x-\frac{5}{2}a$.
  Since the two lines intersect at $(3a,-a)$, we have $\frac{3}{2}a=-\frac{5}{2}a+b$.
  Solving for $b$, we get $b=4a$.
  Therefore, the equation of the line is $y=-\frac{1}{2}x+4a$.
  The equation can be rewritten as $x+2y=8a$.
  Comparing this equation with the given choices, we see that the answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(D)}\ 2x-y=7a}$.

  B: $\quad 200$
  C: $\quad 2,000$
  D: 20,000
Response 0:

Question: A circle in the $x y$-plane has center $(5,7)$ and radius 2. Which of the following is an equation of the circle?
Choices:
  A: $(x-5)^{2}+(y-7)^{2}=4$
  B: $(x+5)^{2}+(y+7)^{2}=4$
  C: $(x-5)^{2}+(y-7)^{2}=2$
  D: $(x+5)^{2}+(y+7)^{2}=2$

Question: On Saturday afternoon, Armand sent $m$ text messages each hour for 5 hours, and Tyrone sent $p$ text messages each hour for 4 hours. Which of the following represents the total number of messages sent by Armand and Tyrone on Saturday afternoon?

  B: $20 m p$

  A: $-2.2 x^{2}+1.6$
  B: $-2.2 x^{2}+11.2$
  C: $-2.95 x^{2}-7.2 x+12.16$
  D: $-2.95 x^{2}-7.2 x+0.64$

  $= 2.25x^2 - 7.2x + 5.76 - 5.2x^2 + 6.4$
  $= -2.95x^2 - 7.2x + 12.16$
  Therefore, the answer is C: $-2.95 x^{2}-7.2 x+12.16$.

### Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 26 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: In the $x y$-plane, the line determined by the points $(2, k)$ and $(k, 32)$ passes through the origin. Which of the following could be the value of $k$ ?
Choices:
  A: 0
  B: 4
  C: 8
  D: 16
Response 0:
Thought:
  If the line passes through the origin, then the coordinates of both points must satisfy the equation of the line.
  The equation of the line passing through two points $(x_1, y_1)$ and $(x_2, y_2)$ is given by:
  $y - y_1 = \frac{y_2 - y_1}{x_2 - x_1}(x - x_1)$
  If the line passes through the origin, then $(0, 0)$ must satisfy the equation of the line.
  Substituting $(2, k)$ and $(k, 32)$ into the equation of the line and setting $x = 0$ and $y = 0$, we get:
  $k = \frac{k - 32}{2}$ and $32 = \frac{32 - y_1}{x_2 - k}k$
  Solving the first equation, we get $k = -16$.
  Substituting $k = -16$ into the second equation, we get $y_1 = -16$.
  Therefore, $k$ cannot be any of the given choices.
  The answer is None of the Above.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")
Response 1:
Thought:
  If the line passes through the origin, then the two points $(2, k)$ and $(k, 32)$ must be on the same line that passes through the origin.
  The slope of the line passing through the origin and $(2, k)$ is $k/2$.
  The slope of the line passing through the origin and $(k, 32)$ is $32/k$.
  Since the two points are on the same line, the slopes must be equal.
  Therefore, $k/2 = 32/k$.
  Multiplying both sides by $2k$ gives $k^2 = 64$.
  Therefore, $k$ could be $\pm 8$.
  Among the choices, the possible value of $k$ is C: 8.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Thought:
  We know that the line passes through the origin, so the coordinates of both points must satisfy the equation of the line.
  The equation of the line passing through two points $(x_1, y_1)$ and $(x_2, y_2)$ is given by:
  $y - y_1 = \frac{y_2 - y_1}{x_2 - x_1}(x - x_1)$
  If the line passes through the origin, then $(0,0)$ must satisfy the equation of the line.
  Substituting $(2,k)$ and $(k,32)$ into the equation of the line, we get:
  $y - k = \frac{32 - k}{k - 2}(x - 2)$ and $y - 32 = \frac{32 - k}{k - 2}(x - k)$
  Substituting $(0,0)$ into the equation of the line, we get:
  $0 - k = \frac{32 - k}{k - 2}(0 - 2)$ and $0 - 32 = \frac{32 - k}{k - 2}(0 - k)$
  Simplifying these equations, we get:
  $k = \frac{64}{k - 2}$ and $32k - k^2 = 0$
  Solving for $k$ in the second equation, we get $k = 0$ or $k = 32$.
  Substituting $k = 0$ into the first equation, we get $0 = 0$, which is true.
  Substituting $k = 32$ into the first equation, we get $y - 32 = \frac{32 - 32}{k - 2}(x - k)$, which simplifies to $y = 32$.
  Therefore, the only possible value of $k$ is 0.
Action: Answer("A")

  If the line passes through the origin, then the point $(0,0)$ must be on the line.
  The slope of the line is $\frac{32-k}{k-2}$.

Question: If 50 one-cent coins were stacked on top of each other in a column, the column would be approximately $3 \frac{7}{8}$ inches tall. At this rate, which of the following is closest to the number of one-cent coins it would take to make an 8-inch-tall column?
Choices:
  A: 75
  B: 100
  C: 200
  D: 390
Response 0:
Thought:
  50 one-cent coins make a $3 \frac{7}{8}$ inches tall column.
  To find out how many coins it would take to make an 8-inch-tall column, we need to set up a proportion.
  Let x be the number of coins needed to make an 8-inch-tall column.
  We can set up the proportion: $\frac{50}{3 \frac{7}{8}} = \frac{x}{8}$
  We can convert $3 \frac{7}{8}$ to an improper fraction: $3 \frac{7}{8} = \frac{31}{8}$
  We can cross-multiply to solve for x: $50 \times 8 = x \times \frac{31}{8}$
  Simplifying the equation: $x = \frac{50 \times 8 \times 8}{31}$
  Rounding to the nearest whole number, we get x = 103.
  Therefore, the closest answer choice is B: 100.

Question: A customer paid $\$ 53.00$ for a jacket after a 6 percent sales tax was added. What was the price of the jacket before the sales tax was added?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 47.60$
  B: $\$ 50.00$
  C: $\$ 52.60$
  D: $\$ 52.84$
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Let's assume the price of the jacket before the sales tax was added is $x$.
  The sales tax is 6% of the price of the jacket before the tax was added.
  So, the amount of sales tax paid is $0.06x$.
  The total cost of the jacket is the sum of the price of the jacket before the tax was added and the sales tax paid.
  Therefore, we can write the equation: $x + 0.06x = 53.00$
  Solving for $x$, we get $x = \frac{53.00}{1.06} \approx 50.00$
  Therefore, the price of the jacket before the sales tax was added is $\$ 50.00$.
  The answer is B: $\$ 50.00$.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's assume the price of the jacket before the sales tax was added is $x$.
  The sales tax rate is 6%, which means the tax is 6% of $x$.
  The total price the customer paid is the sum of the price of the jacket and the sales tax, which is $x + 0.06x = 1.06x$.
  We know that the customer paid $\$ 53.00$, so we can set up the equation $1.06x = 53$ and solve for $x$.
  $1.06x = 53 \Rightarrow x = \frac{53}{1.06} \approx 50$
  Therefore, the price of the jacket before the sales tax was added is $\$ 50.00$.

Question: The world's population has grown at an average rate of 1.9 percent per year since 1945. There were approximately 4 billion people in the world in 1975. Which of the following functions represents the world's population $P$, in billions of people, $t$ years since $1975 ?(1$ billion $=1,000,000,000)$
Choices:
  A: $P(t)=4(1.019)^{t}$
  B: $P(t)=4(1.9)^{t}$
  C: $P(t)=1.19 t+4$
  D: $P(t)=1.019 t+4$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The population has grown at an average rate of 1.9% per year since 1945.
  The population in 1975 was approximately 4 billion people.
  We can use the formula for exponential growth, which is $P(t)=P_{0}(1+r)^{t}$, where $P_{0}$ is the initial population, $r$ is the annual growth rate, and $t$ is the time in years.
  We can substitute $P_{0}=4$ and $r=0.019$ into the formula.
  Therefore, the function that represents the world's population $P$, in billions of people, $t$ years since $1975$ is $P(t)=4(1.019)^{t}$.
  The answer is A: $P(t)=4(1.019)^{t}$.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:

  We know that P(0) = 4 billion and r = 0.019.
  Therefore, the function is P(t) = 4 * (1 + 0.019)^t = 4 * 1.019^t.
  The answer is A: $P(t)=4(1.019)^{t}$.

### Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 34 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: If a white birch tree and a pin oak tree each now have a diameter of 1 foot, which of the following will be closest to the difference, in inches, of their diameters 10 years from now? $(1$ foot $=12$ inches $)$
Choices:
  A: 1.0
  B: 1.2
  C: 1.3
  D: 1.4
Response 0:
Thought:
  We can use the formula $d=kt+c$ to estimate the diameter of a tree, where $d$ is the diameter of the tree, $t$ is the time in years, $k$ is the growth rate, and $c$ is the initial diameter of the tree.
  We can assume that the growth rate of the white birch tree is $k_1=0.1$ and the growth rate of the pin oak tree is $k_2=0.15$.
  We can also assume that the initial diameter of both trees is $c=12$ inches.
  Therefore, the diameter of the white birch tree after 10 years is $d_1=0.1\times10+12=13$ inches, and the diameter of the pin oak tree after 10 years is $d_2=0.15\times10+12=13.5$ inches.
  The difference in their diameters after 10 years is $d_2-d_1=13.5-13=0.5$ inches.
  The answer is not one of the choices, so we need to select the closest one.
  The closest choice is C: 1.3.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The white birch tree and the pin oak tree will grow at different rates.
  The white birch tree grows at a rate of 6 inches per year.
  The pin oak tree grows at a rate of 9 inches per year.
  In 10 years, the white birch tree will have grown $6 \times 10 = 60$ inches.
  In 10 years, the pin oak tree will have grown $9 \times 10 = 90$ inches.
  The difference in their diameters will be the difference in their radii, which is half the difference in their diameters.
  The difference in their radii will be $\frac{90-60}{2}=15$ inches.
  Therefore, the answer is $\frac{15}{12}=1.25$ feet.
  The closest answer choice to 1.25 is 1.3.

  The diameter of a circle is twice its radius, so $r = \frac{d}{2}$, where $d$ is the diameter of the circle.
  Therefore, $C = \pi d$.
  If we assume that the trees will grow in a way that maintains their circular shape, then we can estimate the difference in their diameters 10 years from now by finding the difference in their circumferences 10 years from now.
  Let $d_1$ be the diameter of the white birch tree now, and let $d_2$ be the diameter of the pin oak tree now.
  Let $c_1$ be the circumference of the white birch tree 10 years from now, and let $c_2$ be the circumference of the pin oak tree 10 years from now.
  Then $c_1 = \pi (d_1 + 10)$ and $c_2 = \pi (d_2 + 10)$.
  The difference in their circumferences 10 years from now is $c_2 - c_1 = \pi (d_2 + 10) - \pi (d_1 + 10) = \pi (d_2 - d_1)$.
  The difference in their diameters 10 years from now is $\frac{1}{\pi} (c_2 - c_1) = d_2 - d_1$.
  Therefore, the answer is the difference in their diameters, which is the same as the difference in their circumferences 10 years from now, which is $\frac{1}{\pi} (c_2 - c_1) = d_2 - d_1$.
  We don't know the exact values of $d_1$ and $d_2$, but we can use the fact that they are both 1 foot now to estimate their difference.
  If we assume that they will each grow by the same amount over the next 10 years, then their difference in diameter 10 years from now will be the same as their difference in diameter now, which is 0.
  Therefore, the answer is closest to 0.
  The answer is A: 1.0.

  B: $8 x y^{2}-6 y^{2}$
  C: $2 x^{2} y+2 x y^{2}$
  D: $2 x^{2} y+8 x y^{2}-6 y^{2}$

  $$= x^{2} y-3 y^{2}+5 x y^{2}+x^{2} y-3 x y^{2}+3 y^{2}$$
  $$= 2x^{2}y+2xy^{2}$$
  Therefore, the answer is C: $2 x^{2} y+2 x y^{2}$.

### Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 36 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A company purchased a machine valued at $\$ 120,000$. The value of the machine depreciates by the same amount each year so that after 10 years the value will be $\$ 30,000$. Which of the following equations gives the value, $v$, of the machine, in dollars, $t$ years after it was purchased for $0 \leq t \leq 10 ?$
Choices:
  A: $v=30,000-9,000 t$
  B: $v=120,000-9,000 t$
  C: $v=120,000+9,000 t$
  D: $v=120,000-30,000 t$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The value of the machine depreciates by the same amount each year.
  After 10 years, the value of the machine will be $\$ 30,000$.
  The initial value of the machine is $\$ 120,000$.
  The value of the machine decreases linearly over time.
  Therefore, the equation of the line that represents the value of the machine over time is of the form $v = mt + b$.
  We can use the two points $(0, 120000)$ and $(10, 30000)$ to find the slope $m$ and the y-intercept $b$ of the line.
  The slope $m$ is equal to the change in value over the change in time, which is $\frac{30000-120000}{10-0} = -9000$.
  The y-intercept $b$ is equal to the initial value of the machine, which is $\$ 120,000$.
  Therefore, the equation that gives the value of the machine, $v$, in dollars, $t$ years after it was purchased is $v = 120,000 - 9,000t$.
  The answer is B: $v=120,000-9,000 t$.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The value of the machine depreciates by the same amount each year.
  After 10 years, the value of the machine will be $\$ 30,000$.
  The initial value of the machine is $\$ 120,000$.
  The value of the machine decreases linearly over time.
  Therefore, the equation of the line that represents the value of the machine over time is of the form $v = mt + b$, where $m$ is the slope and $b$ is the initial value.
  The slope of the line is $\frac{30,000 - 120,000}{10 - 0} = -9,000$.
  The initial value of the line is $120,000$.
  Therefore, the equation of the line is $v = -9,000t + 120,000$.
  The answer is B: $v=120,000-9,000 t$.

### Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 37 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$\begin{aligned}& x=y-3 \\& \frac{x}{2}+2 y=6\end{aligned}$$Which ordered pair $(x, y)$ satisfies the system of equations shown above?
Choices:
  A: $(-3,0)$
  B: $(0,3)$
  C: $(6,-3)$
  D: $(36,-6)$
Response 0:
Thought:
  We can solve the system of equations by substitution or elimination method.
  Let's use substitution method.
  We have x in terms of y in the first equation, so we can substitute it in the second equation.
  $$\frac{x}{2}+2 y=6$$
  $$\frac{y-3}{2}+2 y=6$$
  $$y-3+4y=12$$
  $$5y=15$$
  $$y=3$$
  Now we can substitute y=3 in the first equation to find x.
  $$x=y-3$$
  $$x=3-3$$
  $$x=0$$
  Therefore, the ordered pair $(x,y)$ that satisfies the system of equations is (0,3).
  The answer is B: $(0,3)$.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:

Simplifying this equation, we get $x=0$.
Substituting this value of $x$ in the first equation, we get $y=3$.
Therefore, the ordered pair $(x,y)$ that satisfies the system of equations is $(0,3)$.

  Solving for y, we get $y=3$.
  Substituting $y=3$ into the first equation, we get $x=0$.
  Therefore, the ordered pair $(x,y)$ that satisfies the system of equations is $(0,3)$.
  The answer is B: $(0,3)$.
Response 9:

  We can solve for the other variable.
  We can substitute the value of that variable back into the first equation to find the value of the other variable.
  We can check which ordered pair satisfies both equations.

  Substituting $y=3$ into the first equation gives $x=0$.

### Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 38 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Ken is working this summer as part of a crew on a farm. He earned $\$ 8$ per hour for the first 10 hours he worked this week. Because of his performance, his crew leader raised his salary to $\$ 10$ per hour for the rest of the week. Ken saves $90 \%$ of his earnings from each week. What is the least number of hours he must work the rest of the week to save at least $\$ 270$ for the week?
Choices:
  A: 38
  B: 33
  C: 22
  D: 16
Response 0:
Thought:
  Ken earned $\$ 8$ per hour for the first 10 hours, so he earned $\$ 8 \cdot 10 = \$ 80$.
  Let $h$ be the number of hours he must work the rest of the week to save at least $\$ 270$ for the week.
  He earned $\$ 10$ per hour for the rest of the week, so he earned $\$ 10h$.
  He saves $90 \%$ of his earnings from each week, so he saves $0.9(\$ 80 + \$ 10h) = \$ 72 + \$ 9h$.
  We need to solve the inequality $\$ 72 + \$ 9h \geq \$ 270$ for $h$.
  Simplifying the inequality, we get $h \geq \frac{198}{9}$.
  The least integer greater than or equal to $\frac{198}{9}$ is $22$.
  Therefore, Ken must work at least $22$ hours the rest of the week to save at least $\$ 270$ for the week.
  The answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(C) }22}$.

Question: A cargo helicopter delivers only 100-pound packages and 120-pound packages. For each delivery trip, the helicopter must carry at least 10 packages, and the total weight of the packages can be at most 1,100 pounds. What is the maximum number of 120-pound packages that the helicopter can carry per trip?
Choices:
  A: 2
  B: 4
  C: 5
  D: 6
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume that the helicopter carries x 100-pound packages and y 120-pound packages.
  We know that the helicopter must carry at least 10 packages, so x + y >= 10.
  We also know that the total weight of the packages can be at most 1,100 pounds, so 100x + 120y <= 1100.
  We want to find the maximum value of y.
  We can solve this problem using linear programming.
  The objective function is y, and the constraints are x + y >= 10 and 100x + 120y <= 1100.
  We can convert the constraints into slope-intercept form: y >= -x + 10 and y <= (-5/6)x + 55/6.
  The feasible region is a polygon with vertices at (0,10), (6,4), and (11,0).
  The maximum value of y occurs at the vertex (6,4), so the maximum number of 120-pound packages that the helicopter can carry per trip is 4.
  Therefore, the answer is B: 4.

Question: Kathy is a repair technician for a phone company. Each week, she receives a batch of phones that need repairs. The number of phones that she has left to fix at the end of each day can be estimated with the equation $P=108-23 d$, where $P$ is the number of phones left and $d$ is the number of days she has worked that week. What is the meaning of the value 108 in this equation?
Choices:
  A: Kathy will complete the repairs within 108 days.
  B: Kathy starts each week with 108 phones to fix.
  C: Kathy repairs phones at a rate of 108 per hour.
  D: Kathy repairs phones at a rate of 108 per day.
Response 0:
Thought:
  The equation is in the form of $P=108-23d$.
  The coefficient of $d$ is -23, which means that the number of phones left to fix decreases by 23 each day.
  When $d=0$, $P=108$, which means that Kathy starts each week with 108 phones to fix.
  Therefore, the meaning of the value 108 in this equation is that Kathy starts each week with 108 phones to fix.
  The answer is B: Kathy starts each week with 108 phones to fix.

Topic: Math
Question: In the $x y$-plane, the graph of which of the following equations is a line with a slope of 3 ?
Choices:
  A: $y=\frac{1}{3} x$
  B: $y=x-3$
  C: $y=3 x+2$
  D: $y=6 x+3$
Response 0:

  0&=16a+4b+c \\
  -2&=25a+5b+c \\
  \end{align*}

Question: Which of the following complex numbers is equal to $(5+12 i)-\left(9 i^{2}-6 i\right)$, for $i=\sqrt{-1}$ ?
Choices:
  A: $-14-18 i$
  B: $-4-6 i$
  C: $4+6 i$
  D: $14+18 i$
Response 0:
Thought:
We know that $i^{2}=-1$. Therefore, $9i^{2}-6i=9(-1)-6i=-9-6i$. 
So, $(5+12i)-(9i^{2}-6i)=(5+12i)-(-9-6i)=(5+12i+9+6i)=(14+18i)$.
Therefore, the answer is D: $14+18i$.

### Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 45 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: In the $x y$-plane, the parabola with equation $y=(x-11)^{2}$ intersects the line with equation $y=25$ at two points, $A$ and $B$. What is the length of $\overline{A B}$ ?
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 12
  C: 14
  D: 16
Response 0:
Thought:
  We need to find the $x$-coordinates of the points $A$ and $B$ where the parabola intersects the line $y=25$.
  Setting $y=25$ in the equation of the parabola, we get $25=(x-11)^2$.
  Taking the square root of both sides, we get $x-11=\pm 5$.
  So, $x=6$ or $x=16$.
  Therefore, the $x$-coordinates of the points $A$ and $B$ are $6$ and $16$.
  The distance between $A$ and $B$ is $16-6=10$.
  Therefore, the length of $\overline{A B}$ is $10$.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  We need to find the $x$-coordinates of the points where the parabola intersects the line $y=25$.
  We can set $(x-11)^2 = 25$ and solve for $x$.
  $(x-11)^2 = 25$ can be rewritten as $(x-11)(x-11) = 25$.
  Therefore, $x-11 = \pm 5$.
  So, $x = 6$ or $x = 16$.
  These are the $x$-coordinates of points $A$ and $B$.
  The length of $\overline{AB}$ is the difference between the $x$-coordinates of $A$ and $B$.
  Therefore, the length of $\overline{AB}$ is $16-6=10$.
  The answer is A: 10.
Action: Answer("A")

Question: Oil and gas production in a certain area dropped from 4 million barrels in 2000 to 1.9 million barrels in 2013. Assuming that the oil and gas production decreased at a constant rate, which of the following linear functions $f$ best models the production, in millions of barrels, $t$ years after the year 2000 ?
Choices:
  A: $f(t)=\frac{21}{130} t+4$
  B: $f(t)=\frac{19}{130} t+4$
  C: $f(t)=-\frac{21}{130} t+4$
  D: $f(t)=-\frac{19}{130} t+4$
Response 0:
Thought:
  We can use the slope-intercept form of a linear equation to model the production.
  The slope of the line is the rate of change of the production.
  The production decreased from 4 million barrels in 2000 to 1.9 million barrels in 2013, which is a decrease of 2.1 million barrels over 13 years.
  Therefore, the rate of change of the production is $\frac{-2.1}{13}=-\frac{21}{130}$ million barrels per year.
  The y-intercept of the line is the initial production in 2000, which is 4 million barrels.
  Therefore, the linear function that models the production is $f(t)=-\frac{21}{130}t+4$.
  The answer is C: $f(t)=-\frac{21}{130} t+4$.
Action: Answer("C")

Topic: Math
Question: Townsend Realty purchased the Glenview Street property and received a $40 \%$ discount off the original price along with an additional $20 \%$ off the discounted price for purchasing the property in cash. Which of the following best approximates the original price, in dollars, of the Glenview Street property?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 350,000$
  B: $\$ 291,700$
  C: $\$ 233,300$
  D: $\$ 175,000$
Response 0:
Thought:
Let's assume the original price of the property is $x$ dollars.
Townsend Realty received a $40 \%$ discount off the original price, which means they paid $60 \%$ of the original price.
The price after the $40 \%$ discount is $0.6x$ dollars.
Townsend Realty received an additional $20 \%$ off the discounted price for purchasing the property in cash.
The price after the additional $20 \%$ discount is $0.8(0.6x) = 0.48x$ dollars.
We need to find the original price of the property, which is $x$ dollars.
We can set up an equation: $0.48x = x - 0.4x$.
Solving for $x$, we get $x = 83333.33$ dollars (rounded to the nearest cent).
The answer that best approximates the original price, in dollars, of the Glenview Street property is C: $\$ 233,300$.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
Let the original price of the property be $x$.
Townsend Realty received a $40 \%$ discount off the original price, so they paid $60 \%$ of the original price.
They also received an additional $20 \%$ off the discounted price for purchasing the property in cash, so they paid $80 \%$ of the discounted price.
Therefore, the price Townsend Realty paid is $0.8 \times 0.6 x = 0.48 x$.
We need to find the original price $x$.
We know that $0.48 x$ is the price Townsend Realty paid, which is the discounted price after the two discounts.
Therefore, we can find the original price by dividing the discounted price by $0.6$ (the percentage of the original price Townsend Realty paid after the first discount).
So, $x = \dfrac{0.48 x}{0.6} = 0.8x$.
Solving for $x$, we get $x = \boxed{\textbf{(C)}\ \$233,300}$.

Question: The formula below is often used by project managers to compute $E$, the estimated time to complete a job, where $O$ is the shortest completion time, $P$ is the longest completion time, and $M$ is the most likely completion time.$$E=\frac{O+4 M+P}{6}$$Which of the following correctly gives $P$ in terms of $E, O$, and $M$ ?
Choices:
  A: $P=6 E-O-4 M$
  B: $P=-6 E+O+4 M$
  C: $P=\frac{O+4 M+E}{6}$
  D: $P=\frac{O+4 M-E}{6}$
Response 0:
Thought:
  To solve for $P$, we need to isolate $P$ on one side of the equation.
  Multiply both sides of the equation by 6 to eliminate the denominator.
  Distribute the 4 to $M$.
  Then, isolate $P$ by subtracting $O$ and $4M$ from both sides.
  The resulting equation should be $P$ in terms of $E$, $O$, and $M$.
  The answer is A: $P=6 E-O-4 M$.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  To solve for $P$, we need to isolate $P$ on one side of the equation.
  Multiply both sides of the equation by 6 to eliminate the denominator.
  Distribute the 4 to $M$ and simplify.
  Subtract $O$ from both sides of the equation.
  The resulting equation should give $P$ in terms of $E, O$, and $M$.
  The correct answer should be the equation that matches the result of these steps.
  
Action: Answer("A") 

Solution:
  Multiply both sides of the equation by 6:
  $$6E=O+4M+P$$
  Distribute the 4 to $M$:
  $$6E=O+4M+P$$
  $$6E-O-4M=P$$
  Subtract $O$ from both sides of the equation:
  $$P=6E-O-4M$$
  Therefore, the answer is A: $P=6E-O-4M$.

### Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 49 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: \begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|c|c|}\hline$x$ & $f(x)$ \\\hline1 & 5 \\\hline3 & 13 \\\hline5 & 21 \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}Some values of the linear function $f$ are shown in the table above. Which of the following defines $f$ ?
Choices:
  A: $f(x)=2 x+3$
  B: $f(x)=3 x+2$
  C: $f(x)=4 x+1$
  D: $f(x)=5 x$
Response 0:
Thought:
  We can use the given values to find the slope of the function.
  The slope of a linear function is the change in $y$ divided by the change in $x$.
  The change in $y$ from $5$ to $13$ is $13-5=8$.
  The change in $x$ from $1$ to $3$ is $3-1=2$.
  Therefore, the slope of the function is $\frac{8}{2}=4$.
  We can use the slope and one point to find the y-intercept of the function.
  Using the point $(1,5)$, we can write the equation of the function as $f(x)=4x+1$.
  Therefore, the answer is C: $f(x)=4 x+1$.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  To determine the equation of a linear function, we need to find its slope and y-intercept.
  We can find the slope by calculating the difference in y-coordinates divided by the difference in x-coordinates between two points on the line.
  Let's use the points (1, 5) and (3, 13) to find the slope of the line.
  The difference in y-coordinates is 13 - 5 = 8, and the difference in x-coordinates is 3 - 1 = 2.
  Therefore, the slope of the line is 8/2 = 4.
  Now, we can use the point-slope form of a linear equation to find the y-intercept.
  Let's use the point (1, 5) and the slope we just found, which is 4.
  The point-slope form of a linear equation is $y - y_1 = m(x - x_1)$, where $m$ is the slope and $(x_1, y_1)$ is a point on the line.
  Plugging in the values we have, we get $y - 5 = 4(x - 1)$.
  Simplifying this equation, we get $y = 4x + 1$.
  Therefore, the answer is C: $f(x) = 4x + 1$.

Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Thought:
  We can use the given values to find the slope of the line.
  The slope of the line is the change in $f(x)$ divided by the change in $x$.
  The change in $f(x)$ from $5$ to $13$ is $13-5=8$.
  The change in $x$ from $1$ to $3$ is $3-1=2$.
  Therefore, the slope of the line is $\frac{8}{2}=4$.
  We can use the slope and one point to find the $y$-intercept.
  We can use the point $(1,5)$ since it is the easiest to work with.
  Using the point-slope form of a line, we have $f(x)-5=4(x-1)$.
  Simplifying, we get $f(x)=4x+1$.
  Therefore, the answer is C: $f(x)=4 x+1$.
Action: Answer("C")

  Using the points $(1,5)$ and $(3,13)$, we can find the slope of the line as follows:
  slope $= \frac{\text{change in }y}{\text{change in }x} = \frac{13-5}{3-1} = 4$
  Therefore, the equation of the line is $f(x) = 4x+b$, where $b$ is the $y$-intercept of the line.
  We can use the point $(1,5)$ to find $b$ as follows:
  $5 = 4(1) + b \Rightarrow b = 1$
  Therefore, the equation of the line is $f(x) = 4x+1$.
  The answer is C: $f(x)=4x+1$.

Question: Dreams Recalled during One Week\begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|l|c|c|c|c|}\hline& None & 1 to 4 & 5 or more & Total \\\hline\hlineGroup X & 15 & 28 & 57 & 100 \\\hlineGroup Y & 21 & 11 & 68 & 100 \\\hlineTotal & 36 & 39 & 125 & 200 \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}The data in the table above were produced by a sleep researcher studying the number of dreams people recall when asked to record their dreams for one week. Group X consisted of 100 people who observed early bedtimes, and Group Y consisted of 100 people who observed later bedtimes. If a person is chosen at random from those who recalled at least 1 dream, what is the probability that the person belonged to Group Y ?
Choices:
  A: $\frac{68}{100}$
  B: $\frac{79}{100}$
  C: $\frac{79}{164}$
  D: $\frac{164}{200}$
Response 0:
Thought:
  We want to find the probability of choosing a person from Group Y given that the person recalled at least one dream.
  We can find the total number of people who recalled at least one dream by adding the number of people who recalled 1 to 4 dreams and the number of people who recalled 5 or more dreams.
  We can find the total number of people who recalled at least one dream by adding the corresponding values for Group X and Group Y.
  We can then find the probability of choosing a person from Group Y given that the person recalled at least one dream by dividing the number of people who belong to both Group Y and the "1 to 4" or "5 or more" dream recall groups by the total number of people who recalled at least one dream.
  Action: Answer("A") $\frac{68}{100}$
Response 1:
Thought:
- We are looking for the probability of choosing a person from Group Y given that the person recalled at least 1 dream.
- We can find the probability by dividing the number of people in Group Y who recalled at least 1 dream by the total number of people who recalled at least 1 dream.
- The total number of people who recalled at least 1 dream is the sum of the number of people in Group X and the number of people in Group Y who recalled at least 1 dream.
- We can find the number of people in Group Y who recalled at least 1 dream by subtracting the number of people in Group Y who did not recall any dreams from the total number of people in Group Y.
- We can find the total number of people who recalled at least 1 dream by subtracting the number of people who did not recall any dreams from the total number of people in both groups.
- Therefore, the probability of choosing a person from Group Y given that the person recalled at least 1 dream is: (number of people in Group Y who recalled at least 1 dream) / (total number of people who recalled at least 1 dream).
- We can calculate this probability as follows:

Calculation:
- Number of people in Group Y who did not recall any dreams = 21
- Number of people in Group Y who recalled at least 1 dream = 100 - 21 = 79
- Total number of people who did not recall any dreams = 36 + 21 = 57
- Total number of people who recalled at least 1 dream = 200 - 36 = 164
- Probability of choosing a person from Group Y given that the person recalled at least 1 dream = (number of people in Group Y who recalled at least 1 dream) / (total number of people who recalled at least 1 dream) = 79 / 164

Question: The weights, in pounds, for 15 horses in a stable were reported, and the mean, median, range, and standard deviation for the data were found. The horse with the lowest reported weight was found to actually weigh 10 pounds less than its reported weight. What value remains unchanged if the four values are reported using the corrected weight?
Choices:
  A: Mean
  B: Median
  C: Range
  D: Standard deviation
Response 0:
Thought:
  The mean, median, range, and standard deviation are all measures of central tendency or dispersion.
  The mean and standard deviation are affected by outliers, while the median and range are not.
  The horse with the lowest reported weight was found to actually weigh 10 pounds less than its reported weight.
  This means that the lowest reported weight was an outlier and would affect the mean and standard deviation.
  However, the median and range would remain unchanged since they are not affected by outliers.
  Therefore, the answer is B: Median.

Question: What value of $x$ satisfies the equation $3 x+3=27$ ?
Choices:
  A: 3
  B: 8
  C: 10
  D: 27

  $3x=24$
  Dividing both sides of the equation by 3, we get:
  $x=8$
  Therefore, the value of $x$ that satisfies the equation is 8.

  $3x = 24$
  Dividing both sides of the equation by 3, we get:
  $x = 8$
  Therefore, the value of $x$ that satisfies the equation is 8.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 8:

  $3x + 3 - 3 = 27 - 3$
  $3x = 24$
  Finally, we can solve for $x$ by dividing both sides of the equation by 3.
  $3x/3 = 24/3$
  $x = 8$
  Therefore, the value of $x$ that satisfies the equation is 8.

Question: Keith modeled the growth over several hundred years of a tree population by estimating the number of the trees' pollen grains per square centimeter that were deposited each year within layers of a lake's sediment. He estimated there were 310 pollen grains per square centimeter the first year the grains were deposited, with a $1 \%$ annual increase in the number of grains per square centimeter thereafter. Which of the following functions models $P(t)$, the number of pollen grains per square centimeter $t$ years after the first year the grains were deposited?
Choices:
  A: $P(t)=310^{t}$
  B: $P(t)=310^{1.01 t}$
  C: $P(t)=310(0.99)^{t}$
  D: $P(t)=310(1.01)^{t}$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The initial number of pollen grains per square centimeter is 310.
  The number of pollen grains per square centimeter increases by $1 \%$ each year.
  Therefore, the function should be an exponential function with an initial value of 310 and a growth factor of $1.01$.
  The function that models the number of pollen grains per square centimeter is $P(t)=310(1.01)^{t}$.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The initial number of pollen grains per square centimeter is 310.
  The annual increase in the number of pollen grains per square centimeter is 1%.
  Therefore, the function that models the number of pollen grains per square centimeter is an exponential function of the form $P(t)=a(1+r)^t$, where $a$ is the initial amount, $r$ is the annual growth rate expressed as a decimal, and $t$ is the time in years.
  The initial amount is 310, and the annual growth rate is 1%, or 0.01.
  Therefore, the function that models the number of pollen grains per square centimeter is $P(t)=310(1+0.01)^t$.
  Simplifying, we get $P(t)=310(1.01)^t$.
  Therefore, the answer is D: $P(t)=310(1.01)^{t}$.

Question: \begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|c|c|c|c|c|c|c|}\hlineList A & 1 & 2 & 3 & 4 & 5 & 6 \\\hlineList B & 2 & 3 & 3 & 4 & 4 & 5 \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}The table above shows two lists of numbers. Which of the following is a true statement comparing list $\mathrm{A}$ and list B ?
Choices:
  A: The means are the same, and the standard deviations are different.
  B: The means are the same, and the standard deviations are the same.
  C: The means are different, and the standard deviations are different.
  D: The means are different, and the standard deviations are the same.
Response 0:
Thought:
  We can find the mean and standard deviation of each list to compare them.
  The mean of list A is $\frac{1+2+3+4+5+6}{6}=3.5$.
  The mean of list B is $\frac{2+3+3+4+4+5}{6}=3.5$.
  The standard deviation of list A is $\sqrt{\frac{(1-3.5)^2+(2-3.5)^2+(3-3.5)^2+(4-3.5)^2+(5-3.5)^2+(6-3.5)^2}{6}}\approx1.71$.
  The standard deviation of list B is $\sqrt{\frac{(2-3.5)^2+(3-3.5)^2+(3-3.5)^2+(4-3.5)^2+(4-3.5)^2+(5-3.5)^2}{6}}\approx0.96$.
  The means are the same, but the standard deviations are different.
  Therefore, the answer is A: The means are the same, and the standard deviations are different.

### Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 57 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$C=75 h+125$$The equation above gives the amount $C$, in dollars, an electrician charges for a job that takes $h$ hours. Ms. Sanchez and Mr. Roland each hired this electrician. The electrician worked 2 hours longer on Ms. Sanchez's job than on Mr. Roland's job. How much more did the electrician charge Ms. Sanchez than Mr. Roland?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 75$
  B: $\$ 125$
  C: $\$ 150$
  D: $\$ 275$
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's start by finding the amount charged by the electrician for Mr. Roland's job.
  Let's assume that the electrician worked for $x$ hours on Mr. Roland's job.
  Therefore, the electrician worked for $(x+2)$ hours on Ms. Sanchez's job.
  Using the equation given, we can find the amount charged by the electrician for Mr. Roland's job as:
  $$C=75h+125$$
  $$C=75x+125$$
  Similarly, we can find the amount charged by the electrician for Ms. Sanchez's job as:
  $$C=75h+125$$
  $$C=75(x+2)+125$$
  We need to find the difference between the amount charged for Ms. Sanchez's job and Mr. Roland's job.
  Therefore, the difference is:
  $$\begin{aligned} 75(x+2)+125-75x-125 &= 75x+150+125-75x-125 \\ &= 75x-75x+275 \\ &= 275 \end{aligned}$$
  Therefore, the electrician charged Ms. Sanchez $\$ 275$ more than Mr. Roland.
  The answer is D: $\$ 275$.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's first find out how many hours the electrician worked for Mr. Roland's job.
  Let $h_R$ be the number of hours the electrician worked for Mr. Roland's job.
  Then, $h_R+2$ is the number of hours the electrician worked for Ms. Sanchez's job.
  We can set up two equations using the given information:
  $C_R=75h_R+125$ is the amount Mr. Roland was charged.
  $C_S=75(h_R+2)+125=75h_R+175$ is the amount Ms. Sanchez was charged.
  The difference between the two charges is $C_S-C_R=75h_R+175-(75h_R+125)=50$.
  Therefore, the answer is $\$50$.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")

  $C=75h+125$
  $C=75x+125$
  We can use the same equation to find the cost of Ms. Sanchez's job.
  $C=75h+125$
  $C=75(x+2)+125$
  $C=75x+150+125$
  $C=75x+275$
  The difference in cost between Ms. Sanchez's job and Mr. Roland's job is:
  $C_{Sanchez}-C_{Roland}=(75x+275)-(75x+125)=150$
  Therefore, the electrician charged Ms. Sanchez $\$150$ more than Mr. Roland.
  The answer is C: $\$150$.

### Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 58 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Context: Energy per Gram of Typical Macronutrients.\begin{center}.\begin{tabular}{|l|c|c|}.\hline.Macronutrient & Food calories & Kilojoules \\.\hline.Protein & 4.0 & 16.7 \\.\hline.Fat & 9.0 & 37.7 \\.\hline.Carbohydrate & 4.0 & 16.7 \\.\hline.\end{tabular}.\end{center}.The table above gives the typical amounts of energy per gram, expressed in both food calories and kilojoules, of the three macronutrients in food.
Question: If the 180 food calories in a granola bar come entirely from $p$ grams of protein, $f$ grams of fat, and $c$ grams of carbohydrate, which of the following expresses $f$ in terms of $p$ and $c$ ?
Choices:
  A: $f=20+\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$
  B: $f=20-\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$
  C: $f=20-\frac{4}{9}(p-c)$
  D: $f=20+\frac{9}{4}(p+c)$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The energy in a granola bar comes from protein, fat, and carbohydrate.
  The energy per gram of protein is 4.0 food calories.
  The energy per gram of fat is 9.0 food calories.
  The energy per gram of carbohydrate is 4.0 food calories.
  Let $p$, $f$, and $c$ be the number of grams of protein, fat, and carbohydrate in the granola bar, respectively.
  The total energy in the granola bar is 180 food calories.
  Therefore, $4p+9f+4c=180$.
  We need to solve for $f$ in terms of $p$ and $c$.
  Rearranging the equation gives $9f=180-4p-4c$.
  Dividing both sides by 9 gives $f=20-\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$.
  Therefore, the answer is B: $f=20-\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$.
Action: Answer("B")

Response 9:
Thought:
  The energy in food calories from protein, fat, and carbohydrate in a granola bar are $4p$, $9f$, and $4c$, respectively.
  The sum of these energies is equal to 180 food calories.
  Therefore, we have the equation $4p+9f+4c=180$.
  We want to solve for $f$ in terms of $p$ and $c$.
  We can rearrange the equation to isolate $f$ by subtracting $4p$ and $4c$ from both sides and then dividing by 9.
  Therefore, we get $f=\frac{180-4p-4c}{9}$.
  We can simplify this expression by factoring out a 4 from the numerator.
  Therefore, we get $f=\frac{4(45-p-c)}{9}$.
  We can simplify this expression further by dividing both the numerator and denominator by 1.
  Therefore, we get $f=20-\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$.
  The answer is B: $f=20-\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$.

Topic: Math
Question: A painter will paint $n$ walls with the same size and shape in a building using a specific brand of paint. The painter's fee can be calculated by the expression $n K \ell h$, where $n$ is the number of walls, $K$ is a constant with units of dollars per square foot, $\ell$ is the length of each wall in feet, and $h$ is the height of each wall in feet. If the customer asks the painter to use a more expensive brand of paint, which of the factors in the expression would change?
Choices:
  A: $h$
  B: $\ell$
  C: $K$
  D: $n$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The expression for the painter's fee is $n K \ell h$.
  The customer wants the painter to use a more expensive brand of paint.
  The cost of the paint is not included in the expression for the painter's fee.
  Therefore, the only factor that would change in the expression is the constant $K$.
  The answer is C: $K$.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The expression for the painter's fee is $n K \ell h$.
  The customer asks the painter to use a more expensive brand of paint.
  The length and height of each wall are not changing.
  Therefore, $\ell$ and $h$ are constant.
  The number of walls $n$ is also constant.
  Therefore, $n$ is constant.
  The only factor that would change is the cost per square foot of the paint, which is represented by the constant $K$.
  Therefore, the answer is C: $K$.

### Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 60 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Context: $$.\begin{aligned}.& S(P)=\frac{1}{2} P+40 \\.& D(P)=220-P.\end{aligned}.$$.The quantity of a product supplied and the quantity of the product demanded in an economic market are functions of the price of the product. The functions above are the estimated supply and demand functions for a certain product. The function $S(P)$ gives the quantity of the product supplied to the market when the price is $P$ dollars, and the function $D(P)$ gives the quantity of the product demanded by the market when the price is $P$ dollars.
Question: At what price will the quantity of the product supplied to the market equal the quantity of the product demanded by the market?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 90$
  B: $\$ 120$
  C: $\$ 133$
  D: $\$ 155$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The quantity of the product supplied to the market will equal the quantity of the product demanded by the market when the supply function equals the demand function.
  Set $S(P) = D(P)$ and solve for $P$.
  $$.\begin{aligned}S(P)&=D(P) \\\frac{1}{2} P+40&=220-P \\P&=133\end{aligned}.$$
  Therefore, the price at which the quantity of the product supplied to the market equals the quantity of the product demanded by the market is $\$133$.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The quantity of the product supplied to the market will equal the quantity of the product demanded by the market when $S(P)=D(P)$.
  We can set the two functions equal to each other and solve for $P$.
  $$\begin{aligned} S(P)&=D(P) \\ \frac{1}{2} P+40&=220-P \\ \frac{3}{2} P&=180 \\ P&=120 \end{aligned}$$
  Therefore, the price at which the quantity of the product supplied to the market equals the quantity of the product demanded by the market is $\$120$.
  The answer is B: $\$120$.
Action: Answer("B")

  D: $\frac{1}{2}$

  Therefore, the value of $\frac{x}{5}$ is 2.

### Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 62 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$\sqrt{k+2}-x=0$$In the equation above, $k$ is a constant. If $x=9$, what is the value of $k$ ?
Choices:
  A: 1
  B: 7
  C: 16
  D: 79
Response 0:
Thought:
  We are given the equation $\sqrt{k+2}-x=0$ and $x=9$.
  We can substitute $x$ with $9$ to get $\sqrt{k+2}-9=0$.
  We can add $9$ to both sides to isolate the square root term to get $\sqrt{k+2}=9$.
  We can square both sides to get $k+2=81$.
  We can subtract $2$ from both sides to get $k=79$.
  Therefore, the value of $k$ is 79.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  We can solve for $k$ by isolating it on one side of the equation.
  Adding $x$ to both sides of the equation gives $\sqrt{k+2}=x$.
  Squaring both sides of the equation gives $k+2=x^2$.
  Substituting $x=9$ gives $k+2=81$.
  Therefore, $k=79$.

Question: $$2 a x-15=3(x+5)+5(x-1)$$In the equation above, $a$ is a constant. If no value of $x$ satisfies the equation, what is the value of $a$ ?
Choices:
  A: 1
  B: 2
  C: 4
  D: 8
Response 0:
Thought:
  Simplifying the equation, we get:
  $$2ax-15=3x+15+5x-5$$
  $$2ax-15=8x+10$$
  $$2ax-8x=15+10$$
  $$x(2a-8)=25$$
  $$x=\frac{25}{2a-8}$$
  Since no value of $x$ satisfies the equation, the denominator of the expression above must be equal to zero.
  $$2a-8=0$$
  $$2a=8$$
  $$a=4$$
  Therefore, the answer is C: 4.

### Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 67 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The function $f$ is defined by $f(x)=(x+3)(x+1)$. The graph of $f$ in the $x y$-plane is a parabola. Which of the following intervals contains the $x$-coordinate of the vertex of the graph of $f$ ?
Choices:
  A: $-4<x<-3$
  B: $-3<x<1$
  C: $1<x<3$
  D: $3<x<4$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The vertex of a parabola is located at the point $(h,k)$ where $h$ is the $x$-coordinate of the vertex and $k$ is the $y$-coordinate of the vertex.
  The standard form of a quadratic function is $f(x)=a(x-h)^2+k$, where $a$ is the coefficient of the quadratic term and $h$ is the $x$-coordinate of the vertex.
  The given function can be expanded to $f(x)=x^2+4x+3$.
  The vertex of the parabola can be found by completing the square or by using the formula $h=-\frac{b}{2a}$, where $b$ is the coefficient of the linear term and $a$ is the coefficient of the quadratic term.
  In this case, $a=1$ and $b=4$, so $h=-\frac{4}{2(1)}=-2$.
  Therefore, the $x$-coordinate of the vertex is $-2$.
  The answer is A: $-4<x<-3$ because $-4<-2<-3$.

Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The vertex of a parabola is located at the minimum or maximum point of the graph.
  The function $f(x)$ is a quadratic function in standard form $f(x)=ax^2+bx+c$.
  The vertex of the parabola is located at $x=-\frac{b}{2a}$.
  The function $f(x)$ can be rewritten as $f(x)=x^2+4x+3$.
  Therefore, the vertex of the parabola is located at $x=-\frac{b}{2a}=-\frac{4}{2}=-2$.
  The answer is A: $-4<x<-3$.

  The vertex of a parabola is at the point where the slope changes from increasing to decreasing.

  The vertex of a parabola with the equation $f(x)=ax^2+bx+c$ is at $x=-\frac{b}{2a}$.
  The function $f(x)=(x+3)(x+1)$ can be expanded to $f(x)=x^2+4x+3$.
  Therefore, the $x$-coordinate of the vertex of the graph of $f$ is $-\frac{b}{2a}=-\frac{4}{2}= -2$.
  The interval that contains $-2$ is $-3<x<1$.
Action: Answer("B")

  B: $-\frac{4}{5}$
  C: $-\frac{2}{3}$
  D: 4

  Add 4 to both sides of the equation to isolate $9x$.
  Simplify $\frac{2}{3}(9x-6)+4$ to $\frac{18}{3}x-4+4$ to get $6x$.
  Set the two expressions for $9x$ equal to each other and solve for $x$.
  $9x-6=6x+6$
  $3x=12$
  $x=4$

  Simplify $3(4)$ to $12$.
  Subtract 2 from 12 to get 10.
  Therefore, the value of $3x-2$ is 10.

### Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 69 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$0.10 x+0.20 y=0.18(x+y)$$Clayton will mix $x$ milliliters of a $10 \%$ by mass saline solution with $y$ milliliters of a $20 \%$ by mass saline solution in order to create an $18 \%$ by mass saline solution. The equation above represents this situation. If Clayton uses 100 milliliters of the $20 \%$ by mass saline solution, how many milliliters of the $10 \%$ by mass saline solution must he use?
Choices:
  A: 5
  B: 25
  C: 50
  D: 100
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's solve for $x$ in the given equation.
  $$0.10 x+0.20 y=0.18(x+y)$$
  $$0.10 x+0.20 y=0.18x+0.18y$$
  $$0.02 x=0.02 y$$
  $$x=y$$
  We know that Clayton uses 100 milliliters of the $20 \%$ by mass saline solution.
  Let's use $y$ to represent the amount of $20 \%$ by mass saline solution Clayton uses.
  Therefore, $y=100$.
  We also know that $x=y$.
  Therefore, $x=100$.
  Clayton must use 100 milliliters of the $10 \%$ by mass saline solution.
  The answer is D: 100.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's solve for $x$ in the given equation.
  $$0.10 x+0.20 y=0.18(x+y)$$
  $$0.10 x+0.20 y=0.18 x+0.18 y$$
  $$0.02 x=0.02 y$$
  $$x=y$$
  Therefore, the amount of $10 \%$ saline solution used must be equal to the amount of $20 \%$ saline solution used.
  If Clayton uses 100 milliliters of the $20 \%$ saline solution, he must use an equal amount of the $10 \%$ saline solution.
  Therefore, Clayton must use 100 milliliters of the $10 \%$ saline solution.
  The answer is D: 100.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Thought:
  We are given that $y=100$.
  We need to solve for $x$.
  We can simplify the equation by distributing $0.18$ on the right side.
  $$0.10 x+0.20 y=0.18(x+y)$$
  $$0.10 x+0.20 \cdot 100=0.18 x+0.18 \cdot 100$$
  $$0.10 x+20=0.18 x+18$$
  We can simplify further by moving all the $x$ terms to one side and all the constant terms to the other side.
  $$0.10 x-0.18 x=18-20$$
  $$-0.08 x=-2$$
  $$x=\frac{-2}{-0.08}=25$$
  Therefore, Clayton must use 25 milliliters of the $10 \%$ by mass saline solution.
  The answer is B: 25.

### Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 70 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: What are the solutions to $3 x^{2}+12 x+6=0 ?$
Choices:
  A: $x=-2 \pm \sqrt{2}$
  B: $x=-2 \pm \frac{\sqrt{30}}{3}$
  C: $x=-6 \pm \sqrt{2}$
  D: $x=-6 \pm 6 \sqrt{2}$
Response 0:
Thought:
  We can solve the quadratic equation $3 x^{2}+12 x+6=0$ by using the quadratic formula.
  The quadratic formula is $x=\frac{-b \pm \sqrt{b^{2}-4 a c}}{2 a}$ where $a$, $b$, and $c$ are the coefficients of the quadratic equation.
  In this case, $a=3$, $b=12$, and $c=6$.
  Substituting these values into the quadratic formula, we get $x=\frac{-12 \pm \sqrt{12^{2}-4 \cdot 3 \cdot 6}}{2 \cdot 3}$.
  Simplifying this expression, we get $x=\frac{-12 \pm \sqrt{96}}{6}$.
  Factoring out $\sqrt{96}$, we get $x=\frac{-12 \pm \sqrt{16 \cdot 6}}{6}$.
  Simplifying further, we get $x=\frac{-12 \pm 4 \sqrt{6}}{6}$.
  Factoring out $4$, we get $x=\frac{-3 \pm \sqrt{6}}{3}$.
  Therefore, the solutions to $3 x^{2}+12 x+6=0$ are $x=\frac{-3 + \sqrt{6}}{3}$ and $x=\frac{-3 - \sqrt{6}}{3}$.
  The answer is none of the above.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")

  Substituting the values, we get $x=\frac{-12 \pm \sqrt{12^{2}-4 \cdot 3 \cdot 6}}{2 \cdot 3}=\frac{-12 \pm \sqrt{72}}{6}=-2 \pm \frac{\sqrt{18}}{3}=-2 \pm \frac{\sqrt{2 \cdot 9}}{3}=-2 \pm \frac{3 \sqrt{2}}{3}=-2 \pm \sqrt{2}$.
  Therefore, the solutions are $x=-2 \pm \sqrt{2}$.
  The answer is A: $x=-2 \pm \sqrt{2}$.

  If t is a multiple of 20, we can use the formula P = 50,000(0.9)^(t/20).
  If t is not a multiple of 20, we can use the formula P = 50,000(0.9)^(20*floor(t/20)).
  The answer is either B or D.
  Let's try t = 40 and see which formula gives the correct answer.
  Using formula B, we get P = 50,000(0.1)^(40/20) = 50,000(0.1)^2 = 500.
  Using formula D, we get P = 50,000(0.9)^(40/20) = 50,000(0.9)^2 = 40,500.
  The correct answer is D.

Topic: Math
Question: A rectangle was altered by increasing its length by 10 percent and decreasing its width by $p$ percent. If these alterations decreased the area of the rectangle by 12 percent, what is the value of $p$ ?
Choices:
  A: 12
  B: 15
  C: 20
  D: 22
Response 0:
Thought:
Let's assume that the original length and width of the rectangle are $l$ and $w$, respectively. Therefore, the original area of the rectangle is $lw$.
After the alterations, the new length of the rectangle is $1.1l$ and the new width is $(1-p/100)w$. Therefore, the new area of the rectangle is $(1.1l)(1-p/100)w$.
We know that the new area of the rectangle is 12% less than the original area. Therefore, we can write the following equation:
$$
(1.1l)(1-p/100)w = 0.88lw
$$
Simplifying this equation, we get:
$$
1.1(1-p/100) = 0.88
$$
Solving for $p$, we get:
$$
p = 20
$$
Therefore, the value of $p$ is 20.

$p = 20$

Question: What is the set of all solutions to the equation $\sqrt{x+2}=-x ?$
Choices:
  A: $\{-1,2\}$
  B: $\{-1\}$
  C: $\{2\}$
  D: There are no solutions to the given equation.
Response 0:
Thought:
  We can start by squaring both sides of the equation to get rid of the square root.
  $\sqrt{x+2}=-x$ can be written as $(\sqrt{x+2})^2=(-x)^2$.
  Simplifying the right-hand side gives $x^2$, and the left-hand side gives $x+2$.
  So we have the equation $x^2=x+2$.
  Rearranging this equation gives $x^2-x-2=0$.
  Factoring the left-hand side gives $(x-2)(x+1)=0$.
  Therefore, the solutions to the equation are $x=2$ and $x=-1$.
  The answer is A: $\{-1,2\}$.

Topic: Math
Question: \begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|l|c|c|}\hline\multicolumn{3}{|c|}{Townsend Realty Group Investments} \\\hlineProperty address & $\begin{array}{c}\text { Purchase price } \\ \text { (dollars) }\end{array}$ & $\begin{array}{c}\text { Monthly rental } \\ \text { price } \\ \text { (dollars) }\end{array}$ \\\hlineClearwater Lane & 128,000 & 950 \\\hlineDriftwood Drive & 176,000 & 1,310 \\\hlineEdgemont Street & 70,000 & 515 \\\hlineGlenview Street & 140,000 & 1,040 \\\hlineHamilton Circle & 450,000 & 3,365 \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}The Townsend Realty Group invested in the five different properties listed in the table above. The table shows the amount, in dollars, the company paid for each property and the corresponding monthly rental price, in dollars, the company charges for the property at each of the five locations. 23The relationship between the monthly rental price $r$, in dollars, and the property's purchase price $p$, in thousands of dollars, can be represented by a linear function. Which of the following functions represents the relationship?
Choices:
  A: $r(p)=2.5 p-870$
  B: $r(p)=5 p+165$
  C: $r(p)=6.5 p+440$
  D: $r(p)=7.5 p-10$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The relationship between the monthly rental price and the property's purchase price can be represented by a linear function.
  We can use the formula for the equation of a line, y = mx + b, where y is the dependent variable, x is the independent variable, m is the slope, and b is the y-intercept.
  The slope of the line represents the rate of change of the dependent variable with respect to the independent variable.
  In this case, the slope represents the rate of change of the monthly rental price with respect to the property's purchase price.
  We can find the slope by calculating the change in the monthly rental price divided by the change in the property's purchase price between any two points on the line.
  We can choose two points from the table and use them to calculate the slope.
  For example, we can use the points (128, 950) and (176, 1310) for the property on Clearwater Lane and Driftwood Drive, respectively.
  The change in the monthly rental price is 1310 - 950 = 360, and the change in the property's purchase price is 176 - 128 = 48.
  Therefore, the slope is 360/48 = 7.5.
  The y-intercept represents the value of the dependent variable when the independent variable is zero.
  In this case, the y-intercept represents the monthly rental price when the property's purchase price is zero, which does not make sense.
  Therefore, the y-intercept should be negative.
  We can use the point (70, 515) for the property on Edgemont Street to find the y-intercept.
  Using the slope of 7.5 and the point (70, 515), we can find the equation of the line.
  The equation is r(p) = 7.5p - 442.5, which simplifies to r(p) = 7.5p - 10.
  Therefore, the answer is D: $r(p)=7.5 p-10$.
Action: Answer("D")

  To find the y-intercept, we can use one of the points and the slope.
  Let's use the point (128, 950).
  We know that y = 7.5x + b, and we can substitute x = 128 and y = 950 to solve for b.
  950 = 7.5(128) + b
  b = -10
  Therefore, the linear function is r(p) = 7.5p - 10.

  B: 10

Question: Nate walks 25 meters in 13.7 seconds. If he walks at this same rate, which of the following is closest to the distance he will walk in 4 minutes?
Choices:
  A: 150 meters
  B: 450 meters
  C: 700 meters
  D: 1,400 meters
Response 0:
Thought:
  Nate walks 25 meters in 13.7 seconds.
  Let's first calculate his speed in meters per second: 25 meters / 13.7 seconds = 1.82 meters per second.
  We want to find the distance he will walk in 4 minutes, which is 240 seconds.
  To find the distance, we can multiply the speed by the time: 1.82 meters per second * 240 seconds = 436.8 meters.
  The answer is closest to 436.8 meters, which is answer choice B.

Thought:

Question: Roberto is an insurance agent who sells two types of policies: a $\$ 50,000$ policy and a $\$ 100,000$ policy. Last month, his goal was to sell at least 57 insurance policies. While he did not meet his goal, the total value of the policies he sold was over $\$ 3,000,000$. Which of the following systems of inequalities describes $x$, the possible number of $\$ 50,000$ policies, and $y$, the possible number of $\$ 100,000$ policies, that Roberto sold last month?
Choices:
  A: $x+y<57$ $50,000 x+100,000 y<3,000,000$
  B: $x+y>57$ $50,000 x+100,000 y>3,000,000$
  C: $x+y<57$ $50,000 x+100,000 y>3,000,000$
  D: $x+y>57$ $50,000 x+100,000 y<3,000,000$

Question: $$\begin{aligned}& b=2.35+0.25 x \\& c=1.75+0.40 x\end{aligned}$$In the equations above, $b$ and $c$ represent the price per pound, in dollars, of beef and chicken, respectively, $x$ weeks after July 1 during last summer. What was the price per pound of beef when it was equal to the price per pound of chicken?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 2.60$
  B: $\$ 2.85$
  C: $\$ 2.95$
  D: $\$ 3.35$
Response 0:
Thought:
  We want to find the value of $x$ when $b=c$.
  We can substitute the given equations to get $2.35+0.25x=1.75+0.40x$.
  We can then solve for $x$ to find the number of weeks after July 1 when the prices are equal.
  Once we have $x$, we can substitute it into either equation to find the price per pound of beef (or chicken) at that time.
Action: 
  $$\begin{aligned}2.35+0.25x&=1.75+0.40x \\0.15x&=0.60 \\x&=4\end{aligned}$$
  When $x=4$, we have $b=2.35+0.25(4)=\$2.35+\$1.00=\$3.35$.
  Therefore, the answer is D: $\$3.35$. Answer("D")

  Substitute $b$ and $c$ in terms of $x$.
  $$\begin{aligned}2.35+0.25 x &= 1.75+0.40 x \\0.15 x &= 0.60 \\x &= 4\end{aligned}$$
  Substitute $x=4$ in $b=2.35+0.25 x$ to find the price per pound of beef.
  $$\begin{aligned}b &= 2.35+0.25 \times 4 \\&= 3.35\end{aligned}$$
  Therefore, the price per pound of beef when it was equal to the price per pound of chicken was $\$ 3.35$.
  The answer is D: $\$ 3.35$.
Action: Answer("D")

  Substituting $x=12$ in the equation for $b$, we get $b=2.35+0.25(12)=\boxed{\$ 5.35}$.

### Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 88 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The first year Eleanor organized a fund-raising event, she invited 30 people. For each of the next 5 years, she invited double the number of people she had invited the previous year. If $f(n)$ is the number of people invited to the fund-raiser $n$ years after Eleanor began organizing the event, which of the following statements best describes the function $f$ ?
Choices:
  A: The function $f$ is a decreasing linear function.
  B: The function $f$ is an increasing linear function.
  C: The function $f$ is a decreasing exponential function.
  D: The function $f$ is an increasing exponential function.
Response 0:
Thought:
  In the first year, Eleanor invited 30 people.
  For the second year, she invited double the number of people she had invited the previous year, which is $2 \times 30 = 60$ people.
  For the third year, she invited double the number of people she had invited the previous year, which is $2 \times 60 = 120$ people.
  For the fourth year, she invited double the number of people she had invited the previous year, which is $2 \times 120 = 240$ people.
  For the fifth year, she invited double the number of people she had invited the previous year, which is $2 \times 240 = 480$ people.
  We can see that the number of people invited is increasing exponentially.
  Therefore, the function $f$ is an increasing exponential function.
  The answer is D: The function $f$ is an increasing exponential function.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  In the first year, Eleanor invited 30 people.
  For the second year, she invited double the number of people from the previous year, which is $2 \times 30 = 60$ people.
  For the third year, she invited double the number of people from the previous year, which is $2 \times 60 = 120$ people.
  This pattern continues for the next 2 years.
  Therefore, the number of people invited to the fund-raiser $n$ years after Eleanor began organizing the event can be represented by the function $f(n) = 30 \times 2^{n}$.
  This is an increasing exponential function.
